Refuting the Objection That Possibility Is Impossible
Razi presents and refutes an objection that possibility is impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's refutation of the objection that possibility is impossible, specifically how he demonstrates that the division of the possible into existent or nonexistent is incomplete.

Core Idea
Possibility is a mental consideration, not a state of existence or nonexistence.

The concept of possibility (imkan) is foundational in kalam. Some object that if something is possible, it must be either existent or nonexistent, and in either case possibility is impossible. Razi responds by showing that this division is not exhaustive and that the essence can be considered without either state.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the first part of the passage where the objection is presented: the possible must be either existent or nonexistent; in both cases possibility is negated. Also note the second formulation involving the cause's presence.
The objection aims to show that possibility leads to contradiction.
2
Examine Razi's first critique
Razi points out that the division into existence and nonexistence is not exhaustive. The essence (mahiyya) can be considered without either, so the objection fails.
This is a classic move: exposing a false dichotomy.
3
Examine Razi's second critique
He then criticizes the second formulation, showing that 'not present' is ambiguous and the division is incomplete.
This reinforces the idea that the objection relies on a flawed logical division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كان معدوماً فهو حال العدم لا يقبل الوجود فلا يحصل إمكان الوجود والعدم ، وإذا استحال الخلو عن الوجود والعدم وكان كل واحد منهما منافيا للامكان كان القول بالإمكان محالا يمكن تقرير هذا السؤال من وجه آخر : وهو أن الممكن إما أن يكون قد حضر معه سبب وجوده أو لم يحضر ، وبالتقدير الأول يجب وبالتقدير الثانى يمتنع فيكون القول بالإمكان ممتنعا (1) أقول : القسمة فى قوله المحكوم عليه بالإمكان إما أن يكون موجوداً أو معدوماً ليست بحاصرة ، لان المفهوم منه أن المحكوم عليه بالإمكان إما أن يكون مع الوجود أو مع العدم ويعوزه قسم آخر وهو أن لا يكون مع أحدهما . وأما قوله : فإن كان موجوداً فهو حال الوجود لا يقبل العدم ، يقال له هذا مسلم ، أما في غير تلك الحال فلم لا يقبل الوجود وليس حال الماهية أما حال الوجود أو حال العدم، لأن هذين الحالين عند اعتبار الماهية مع الغير يمكن أن يقبل أحدهما لا بعينه ، وهذا الامتناع امتناع لاحق بشرط المحمول . وفي التقرير الثانى الذى قال لهيه إن الممكن إما أن يحضر معه سبب وجوده أو لم يحضر أيضاً فيه خلل ؛ لأن لم يحضر يحتمل أن يحضر معه لم يحضر سبب وجوده ، أو لم يحضر لا بسبب وجوده ، ولا لم يحضر سبب وجوده الذي هو سبب عدمه ، فظهر أن الخلل في هذا الكلام كان سبب أن القسمة لم تكن مستوفاة .
And if it is nonexistent, then in the state of nonexistence it cannot accept existence, so the possibility of existence and nonexistence does not occur. And if freedom from existence and nonexistence is impossible, and each of them is incompatible with possibility, then the assertion of possibility is impossible. This question can be formulated in another way: that the possible either has its cause of existence present with it or not. In the first case it is necessary, in the second it is impossible, so the assertion of possibility is impossible. (1) I say: The division in his statement 'what is predicated as possible is either existent or nonexistent' is not exhaustive, because what is understood from it is that what is predicated as possible is either with existence or with nonexistence, and it lacks another division: that it is not with either of them. And as for his statement 'if it is existent, then in the state of existence it cannot accept nonexistence', it is said to him: this is granted, but why should it not accept existence in a state other than that? And the state of the essence is not only the state of existence or the state of nonexistence, because these two states, when considering the essence with something else, it can accept one of them not specifically. And this impossibility is a consequent impossibility conditioned by the predicate. And in the second formulation which he mentioned: 'the possible either has its cause of existence present or not', there is also a flaw; because 'not present' may mean that its cause of existence is not present, or that it is not present without a cause of existence, nor not present without a cause of existence which is the cause of its nonexistence. So it is clear that the flaw in this statement is that the division is not complete.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage presents an objection against the concept of possibility (imkan) and Razi's refutation. The objection argues that if a thing is possible, it must be either existent or nonexistent; if existent, it cannot accept nonexistence; if nonexistent, it cannot accept existence; thus possibility is impossible. A second formulation states that if the cause of existence is present, the possible is necessary; if absent, it is impossible; again possibility is impossible. Razi critiques the division as non-exhaustive, pointing out that the essence (mahiyya) can be considered without either existence or nonexistence, and the impossibility of change is only conditional. He also shows the flaw in the second formulation's dichotomy.

Key Terms
إمكان
ممكن
وجود
عدم
قسمة
ماهية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many think possibility requires the possible thing to be either actually existent or nonexistent, leading to the conclusion that possibility is self-contradictory.
Correction: Razi shows that possibility is a rational judgment about the essence in itself, not requiring actual existence or nonexistence. The division into existence and nonexistence is not exhaustive, as the essence can be considered without either.

Checkpoint
How does Razi show the division in the first objection is incomplete?
A) By asserting that possibility can be both existence and nonexistence.
B) By pointing out that the essence can be considered without either existence or nonexistence.
C) By arguing that the possible must be necessary.
D) By denying the concept of possibility.

Key Takeaway
Possibility is a rational judgment about the essence independent of actual existence or nonexistence; objections based on false dichotomies fail.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about your future possibilities, do you treat them as fixed properties of the world, or do you recognize them as judgments in your mind? How does Razi's insight that possibility is a mental consideration about essences—not about actual states—change the weight you give to your own assessments of what is possible or impossible?
?
The objection in this lesson assumes that possibility must be grounded in either existence or nonexistence. Have you ever assumed that something is impossible simply because you cannot see how it could happen, forgetting that possibility is a judgment about the essence, not a fact about the current state? What would it mean for your trust in God's power to truly believe that possibility is not constrained by the present?
?
Razi shows that a faulty logical division leads to a false conclusion about reality. In your own life, are there areas where you hold an incomplete or false dichotomy—thinking there are only two options when a third exists? How might this lesson train you to examine your own assumptions before concluding something is impossible?

The Third Objection: Possibility as Non-Existent or Existent
Razi refutes the argument that possibility must be either non-existent or existent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third objection that possibility must be either a non-existent or existent attribute, and why Razi refutes both options, concluding that possibility is a mental consideration.

Core Idea
Possibility is not a real attribute; it is a mental consideration that stops when the intellect stops.

This passage presents a third objection against the reality of possibility. If possibility were real, it would have to be either a non-existent or existent attribute. Both options lead to contradictions. The objector then argues that possibility must be a positive attribute, but that too leads to infinite regress. Razi responds by clarifying that possibility is an intellectual concept, not an extramental attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
First, read the Arabic text and its translation to get the overall flow of the argument.
Pay attention to the logical structure: objection, then two horns.
2
Identify the initial dilemma
Notice that the objector claims possibility must be either a non-existent or an existent attribute.
This is a false dichotomy in Razi's view.
3
Follow the refutation of the first horn
Understand why the non-existent option is rejected: it would make possibility the opposite of impossibility, leading to contradiction.
The objector himself argues that one of the opposites must be positive.
4
Examine the two arguments against the second horn
The existent option is attacked from two angles: (1) it leads to the possible being necessary, (2) it leads to infinite regress.
Each argument aims to show absurdity.
5
Understand Razi's final refutation
Razi concludes that possibility is a mental consideration; the regress only occurs as long as the intellect continues to consider it.
Thus, the infinite regress is not actually problematic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثالها : وهو أن الشى لو كان ممكنا لكان إمكانه إما أن يكون وصفا هدميا أو وجوديا ، والأول باطل ؛ لأنه نقيض للا إمكان الذي يصبح حمله على المعدوم ، والمحمول على المعدوم معدوم فيكون الإمكان ثبوتيا ضرورة كون أحد النقيضين وجودياً . والثانى باطل ؛ لأنه لو كان ثبوتيا لزم المحال من وجهين : الأول : أنه إذا كان ثبوتيا كان مساويا لسائر الموجودات في أصل التبرت و مخالفا لها في خصوصية ماهيته المسماة بالإمكان فيكون ثبوته زائداً على ماهيته، فاتصاف ماهيته وجوده إن كان واجباً لذاته كان الإمكان موجوداً واجباً لذاته وهو صفة الممكن والموصوف بالوجود موجود فالممكن موجود ووجوده شرط لقيام ذلك الإمكان به وما كان شرط الوجود ما كان واجباً لذاته كان أولى أن يكون واجباً لذاته فالممكن لذاته واجب لذاته هذا خلف ، وأما إن كان اتصاف ماهيته بوجوده على سبيل الإمكان كان الإمكان إمكان آخر ولام أن يكون إمكان الإمكان زائداً عليه ولزم التسلسل (۲) أقول ما فى قوله فى إبطال كثير الإمكان عدميا فما تبين حاله . وقوله فى الوجه الأول من إبطال كونه ثبوتيا أنه لو كان ممكنا لسكان اتصاف ماهيته بوجوده على سبيل الإمكان وكان الإمكان إمكان آخر ولزم التسلسل ليس بحق ، لأن الإمكان أمر عقلى فمهما اعتبر العقل للإمكان ماهية ووجوداً حصل فيه إمكان إمكان وإنقطع عند انقطاع اعتباره .
Third: that if a thing were possible, its possibility would be either a non-existent attribute or an existent one. The first is invalid because it is the opposite of impossibility (la-imkan) which can be predicated of the non-existent, and what is predicated of the non-existent is non-existent; so possibility must be positive, since one of two opposites must be positive. The second is invalid because if it were positive, an absurdity would follow from two aspects. First: if it is positive, it would be equal to other existents in the essence of positive existence and different from them in the particularity of its quiddity called possibility; so its positivity is additional to its quiddity. So the quiddity being qualified by its existence: if it is necessary by itself, then possibility would be existent, necessary by itself, and it is the attribute of the possible, and the one qualified by existence is existent; so the possible is existent, and its existence is a condition for that possibility to subsist in it; and whatever is a condition for something necessary by itself is more worthy to be necessary by itself; so the possible by itself is necessary by itself—this is a contradiction. But if the quiddity is qualified by its existence as a possible, then possibility would be another possibility, and it would be necessary that the possibility of possibility be additional to it, leading to an infinite regress. (2) I say: What he said in refuting that possibility is non-existent – its state is not clarified. And his statement in the first aspect of refuting that it is positive, that if it were possible, the quiddity would be qualified by its existence as possible, and possibility would be another possibility leading to an infinite regress, is not correct, because possibility is a mental thing; whenever the intellect considers a quiddity and existence for possibility, there occurs in it the possibility of possibility, and it ceases when its consideration ceases.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage presents a third objection: that possibility must be either a non-existent attribute or an existent attribute. The first option is rejected because it would be the opposite of impossibility, which is predicated of the non-existent; so possibility must be positive. The second option is rejected from two angles: (1) if positive, it leads to the possible being necessary by itself, (2) it leads to an infinite regress of possibilities. Razi's refutation points out that possibility is a mental (aqli) consideration; the regress only occurs as long as the intellect continues to consider it, and it stops when consideration stops.

Key Terms
إمكان
وصف عدمي
وصف وجودي
تسلسل
أمر عقلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The infinite regress in possibility is real and impossible, proving possibility cannot be an attribute.
Correction: Razi explains that the regress is only mental and stops when the intellect stops considering possibility as having a quiddity.

Checkpoint
How does Razi respond to the infinite regress argument that would require 'possibility of possibility' ad infinitum?
A) He denies that possibility is a real attribute.
B) He argues the regress is infinite and thus possibility is impossible.
C) He explains that possibility is a mental consideration; the regress stops when consideration stops.
D) He asserts that possibility is a positive attribute anyway.

Key Takeaway
Possibility is not an extramental attribute but a mental consideration; its reality is only in the intellect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the concept of 'possibility' in your own life—like the possibility of attaining a goal—do you treat it as something real outside your mind, or as a mental assessment? How does that affect your motivation or patience?
?
Razi says the infinite regress in possibility stops when the intellect stops. Is there an area of theological reasoning where you have allowed an argument to spiral endlessly in your mind, rather than recognizing it as a mental construct? What would it take for you to stop that regress and submit?
?
If possibility is only a mental consideration, then your entire framework of 'what could happen' is a tool from your intellect. Does that humble you, knowing that your plans and fears are not ultimate realities? How should this reshape your reliance on Allah's decree?

Possibility as an Instrument of the Intellect
Razi explains that possibility is a mental instrument for understanding.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that possibility functions as a mental instrument (āla) for the intellect to reason about possible things, and that it is not itself an object of consideration unless the intellect turns to examine it.

Core Idea
Possibility is a tool for thinking, not a property of things.

In this passage, Imam al-Razi introduces a subtle point (nukta) about the nature of possibility. He explains that when we reason about possible things, we use the concept of possibility as an instrument, much like we use mental images. Only when we turn to examine possibility itself does it become an object of thought, and then it is no longer pure possibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the full translation. Notice the dense style and the key terms: نكتة, آلة, عاقل, معقول.
This passage is a single, continuous argument; read it as a whole.
2
Understand the sky analogy
Razi uses the example of intellecting the sky. The intellect uses the mental form of the sky as an instrument to know the sky itself, without judging the form's own existence. Grasp how this illustrates the distinction between instrument and object.
The form of the sky is not considered for its own properties when used as an instrument.
3
Apply the analogy to possibility
Now see that possibility is like that instrument: when we say something is possible, we use 'possibility' to understand the state of that thing, not to consider possibility itself. Only when we turn to examine possibility does it become an object with its own attributes.
Razi emphasizes that possibility as such is not described as existent or non-existent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وههنا نكتة ينبغى أن تحصل وهو أن كون الشيء معقولا ينظر فيه العقل ويعتبر وجوده ولا وجوده غير كونه آلة للعاقل لا ينظر فيه حيث ينظر فيما هو آلة لتعقله ، بل إنما ينظر به مثلا العاقل يعقل السماء ولا يحكم عليها بحكم بل يعقل أن المعقول بتلك الصورة هو السماء وهو جوهر ، ثم إذا نظر في تلك الصورة أي يجعلها معقولا منظوراً إليها لا آلة في النظر إلى غيرها وجدها عرضاً موجوداً فى محل هو عقله ممكن الوجود . وهكذا الإمكان هو كآلة للعاقل بها يعرف حال الممكن فى أن وجوده كيف يعرض لماهيته ولا ينظر في كون الإمكان موجوداً أو غير موجود أو جوهراً أو عرضاً أو واجبا أو ممكنا ، ثم إن نظر في وجوده أو إمكانه أو وجوبه أو جوهريته أو عرضيته لم يكن بذلك الاعتبار إمكانا لشيء بل كان عرضاً فى محل هو العقل وممكنا في ذاته ووجوده غير ماهيته ، وإذا تقرر هذا فالامكان من حيث هو إمكان لا يوصف بكونه موجوداً أو غير موجود وممكنا أو غير ممكن وإذا وصف بثوء من ذلك لا يكون حينئذ إمكانا بل يكون له إمكان آخر فليحقق هذا حتى ينكشف حملة اعتراضات هذا الفاضل على الإمكان وعلى أمثاله وتزول الحيرة الذي عرضت له . وتعرض لمن تقبع مقالته
And here there is a subtle point that should be grasped: that the thing being intelligible—the intellect considers it and considers its existence and nonexistence—other than its being an instrument for the intellect, it does not consider it where it considers that which is an instrument for its intellection, but rather it considers by means of it. For example, the intellect intellects the sky and does not pass a judgment on it, but it intellects that the intelligible in that form is the sky and it is a substance. Then, when it considers that form—i.e., makes it an intelligible looked at, not an instrument for looking at something else—it finds it to be an existent accident in a locus which is its intellect, possible of existence. And likewise, possibility is like an instrument for the rational being by which he knows the state of the possible, how its existence occurs to its quiddity, and he does not consider whether possibility is existent or non-existent, or substance or accident, or necessary or possible. Then if he considers its existence or its possibility or its necessity or its substantiality or its accidentalness, then by that consideration it is not possibility for something, but rather it is an accident in a locus which is the intellect, and possible in itself, and its existence is other than its quiddity. And if this is established, then possibility, insofar as it is possibility, is not described as being existent or non-existent, or possible or not possible; and if it is described by something of that, it is not then possibility, but it has another possibility. So let this be verified so that the host of objections of this excellent man against possibility and its likes be uncovered, and the confusion that occurred to him be removed. And he [Al-Razi] exposes to those who follow his saying.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory note (nukta) by Razi clarifying the nature of possibility. He analogizes possibility to an instrument (ala) used by the intellect to understand the state of possible things. Just as the intellect uses the form of the sky to understand the sky itself without judging its ontological status, similarly possibility is used to understand how existence occurs to a quiddity. When the intellect turns to examine possibility itself, it becomes an object of consideration and then it is no longer pure possibility but an accident in the mind, having its own possibility. So possibility as such is not describable as existent or non-existent; it is a second-order concept.

Key Terms
نكتة
آلة
عاقل
معقول
عقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Possibility is an attribute that exists in external things, like a property of the possible object.
Correction: Razi teaches that possibility is a mental instrument (āla) used by the intellect to reason about possible things. It is not an ontological attribute of external objects; only when considered itself does it become an accident in the mind.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, when the intellect uses possibility to understand a possible thing, what is the status of possibility itself in that act?
A) It is considered as an object of thought.
B) It is used as an instrument, not considered itself.
C) It is judged to be existent.
D) It is considered as a substance.

Key Takeaway
Possibility, when used to reason about possible things, is a mental instrument; only when examined itself does it become an object with its own possibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever treat the concepts you use in your daily reasoning—like possibility, necessity, or even faith—as if they were concrete things outside your mind? How might that error lead you to doubt or confusion in matters of creed? Commit today to reflect on one theological concept you've struggled with and ask yourself: have I been using it as a tool or treating it as an idol?
?
When you engage in intellectual discussions about Islam, are you aware that even your reasoning tools are gifts from Allah? Or do you unconsciously assume that your mental constructs are absolute realities? How would recognizing this change the humility with which you approach theological debates? This week, before entering a discussion, pause and remind yourself that your understanding of possibility and necessity is but a means—not the end.
?
Al-Razi warns that failing to grasp this subtle point leads to confusion. Have you ever been confused by an objection to a theological argument because you mistook a mental instrument for a real attribute? What would it take for you to trust the framework of the scholars rather than your own unexamined assumptions? Write down one objection you've encountered and re-analyze it using the distinction between instrument and object.

Razi's Refutation of Future Possibility as an Attribute Defense
Razi refutes the defense that possibility is only about future contingency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's argument against the concept of future possibility as a defense for possibility being an attribute.

Core Idea
Future possibility cannot be present now because it depends on a future that does not yet exist.

Razi presents a second objection against the view that possibility is an attribute. He then anticipates a defense based on future possibility and refutes it with an argument that possibility is a relation requiring both relata. This lesson unpacks Razi's careful reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Notice the argument: if possibility were an existent attribute, then a non-existent thing would be qualified by an existent attribute, which is absurd.
2
Understand the defense
Some claim that possibility is about future states, not present ones, so the objection doesn't apply.
3
Examine Razi's first refutation
Razi argues that future possibility cannot be present now because the future hasn't occurred, so the possibility depends on an impossible condition.
If future nonexistence in the present depends on the future, which is not present, it's impossible.
4
Explore the second refutation
Even if one says possibility is about the future, Razi says possibility is a relation that exists only when both terms exist — so it can't exist in the present when the future is absent.
5
Reflect on the implication
Realize that this argument challenges the idea that possibility is a real attribute; it becomes a relative notion.

والثاني : أن المحدث قبل وجوده ممكن لذاته ، فلو كان الإمكان صفة موجودة لكان الشيء حال عدمه موصوفاً بصفة وجوده وذلك محال (1) لا يقال : الجواب عن الإشكال الأول أن ذلك إنما يتوجه على من يقول الشيء حال وجوده ممكن الوجود أو حال عدمه ممكن العدم، أما من يقول حال وجوده يمكن أن يصير معدوماً في الزمان الثاني لا يلزمه هذا الإشكال . وعن الثاني : أنه لا يلزم من صدق قولنا الماهية بشرط كونها موجودة غير قابلة للعدم صدق قولنا الماهية التي هي أحد أجزاء ذلك المجموع غير قابلة للعدم . و من الثالث : أن الإمكان وصف ثابت في الذمن لا تحقق له في الخارج، وعلى هذا التقدير لا يلزم ماذكرتم . لأنا نجيب عن الأول من وجهين : الأول أن القول بالإمكان الاستقبالى محال ، لأنا إذا حكمنا على الموجود في الحال بأنه يمكن أن يعدم فى الاستقبال فإما أن يقال إمكان المدم الاستقبالى حاصل في الحال ، أو يقال إمكان العدم الاستقبالى لا يحصل إلا في الاستقبال ، الأول محال ، لأن العدم فى الاستقبال من حيث إنه في الاستقبال موقوف على حصول الاستقبال ، وحصول الاستقبال محال في الحال فحصول العدم الاستقبالى من حيث إنه عدم استقبالى موقوف على حضور شرط محال والموقوف على المحال محالى ، فالعدم الاستقبالى ممتنع حضوره في الحال ، وإذا استحال حصول العدم الاستقبالى فى الحال لا يمكن حصوله إلا في الاستقبال كان إمكان حصوله حاصلا في الاستقبال لا في الحال . فإن قلت: إنه وإن كان بهذا الشرط ممتنع الحصول في الحال لكنه غير ممتنع في الاستقبال ، ونحن إنما أثبتنا هذا الإمكان بالنسبة إلى الاستقبال قلت : الإمكان نسبة والنسبة لا توجد إلا بعد وجود المنتسبين . فالإمكان بالنسبة إلى الاستقبال لا يوجد إلا عند وجود الاستقبال فحصوله بالحال محال
And the second: that the originated thing before its existence is possible in itself; if possibility were an existent attribute, then the thing in the state of nonexistence would be qualified by an existent attribute, which is absurd. (1) It cannot be said: the answer to the first problem is that this only applies to one who says that the thing in the state of existence is possible of existence or in the state of nonexistence is possible of nonexistence; but for one who says that in the state of existence it can become nonexistent in the second time, this problem does not apply. And about the second: that it does not follow from the truth of our statement 'the quiddity under the condition of being existent is not receptive to nonexistence' the truth of our statement 'the quiddity that is one of the parts of that composite is not receptive to nonexistence'. And about the third: that possibility is an attribute established in the mind, having no realization in external existence, and on this assumption what you mentioned does not follow. For we answer the first from two aspects: first, that the statement about future possibility is impossible, because if we judge of the currently existent that it can become nonexistent in the future, then either it is said that the possibility of future nonexistence is present now, or it is said that the possibility of future nonexistence only occurs in the future. The first is impossible, because future nonexistence, insofar as it is future, depends on the occurrence of the future, and the occurrence of the future is impossible in the present, so the occurrence of future nonexistence insofar as it is future depends on the presence of an impossible condition, and what depends on the impossible is impossible. So future nonexistence is impossible to be present now. And if the occurrence of future nonexistence is impossible in the present, and it cannot occur except in the future, then the possibility of its occurrence occurs in the future, not in the present. If you say: even if it is impossible to occur in the present under this condition, it is not impossible in the future, and we only affirm this possibility with respect to the future. I say: possibility is a relation, and a relation does not exist except after the existence of the two relata. So possibility with respect to the future does not exist except when the future exists, so its occurrence in the present is impossible.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage contains a second objection: an originated thing before existence is possible; if possibility were an attribute, it would be an existent attribute qualifying a non-existent, which is absurd. Then a defense is given: the objection targets those who think possibility is only about present states; others who speak of future possibility are not refuted. Razi's reply: future possibility cannot be present now; it depends on the future existing. He argues that possibility is a relation (nisba) requiring both relata; it cannot exist in the present when the future relatum is absent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Possibility can be a present attribute that qualifies future states.
Correction: Possibility is a relation that requires both relata to exist; if one relatum is future, the possibility exists only when the future exists, not in the present.

Checkpoint
Why does Razi argue that future possibility cannot be present now?
A) Because the future does not exist yet.
B) Because possibility is a relation that requires both relata to exist.
C) Because the future is impossible.
D) Because the present does not have capacity for possibility.

Key Takeaway
Razi shows that possibility is a relation requiring both relata, so future possibility cannot be present; it exists only when the future arrives.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You say 'I will repent tomorrow.' But according to Razi, the possibility of your future repentance does not exist today. That means your intention to repent tomorrow is not a real possibility right now. How does this truth confront your procrastination in turning back to Allah? What will you do within the next hour to make that possibility real?
?
If possibility is a relation that only exists when both its terms exist, then your potential to be among the people of Paradise tomorrow does not exist today except in your present actions. Does your current state reflect that you are actively building that future reality, or are you assuming it will happen without effort? Name one specific action you will take today to move from potential to actual obedience.
?
Razi argues that future nonexistence cannot be present now because it depends on a future that hasn't occurred. Yet many of us live as if our future is already written and secure, forgetting that every future moment is contingent on our present choices. What in your life are you treating as 'already guaranteed' that might actually not happen because you are not acting now to ensure it? What will you change today to align your present with your hopes for the future?

Logic and Technical Terms
intermediate
8 min
Three Objections Against Imkan and the First Reply
Al-Razi enumerates three objections and gives the first part of his answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three objections raised against the reality of imkan and al-Razi's first reply that future-directed possibility is impossible because possibility is a relation requiring both relata to exist.

Core Idea
Possibility is a relation that cannot exist without its relata.

Al-Razi begins by affirming that the originated thing is possible in itself before it exists. A critic then raises three objections: first, that if imkan were a real attribute, it would describe a non-existent thing; second, that an essence on condition of existence is not receptive to non-existence, so imkan is impossible; third, that imkan is merely a mental attribute. Al-Razi first tackles the first objection by arguing that 'future-directed possibility' is incoherent because it would require the future to exist in the present. He then explains that possibility is a relation that only exists when both relata are present.

Guided Path
1
Read the initial statement and three objections
Read from the beginning through the three objections listed after 'لا يقال'. Notice how each objection challenges the reality of imkan.
The critic objects that imkan would attribute something to a non-existent, that conditional necessity blocks imkan, and that imkan is merely mental.
2
Understand the first reply's structure
Al-Razi answers the first objection in two ways. This lesson covers the first way. Read the argument that 'future-directed possibility' is impossible.
He presents two options: either the possibility of future non-existence is present now, or only in the future. Both are argued to be impossible.
3
Grasp the relation argument
After the critic's counterpoint, al-Razi retorts that possibility is a relation (nisba) that only exists when both relata exist. Therefore, future-directed possibility cannot be present now.
This is a key metaphysical principle: relations require their terms to coexist.

والثاني : أن المحدث قبل وجوده ممكن لذاته ، فلو كان الإمكان صفة موجودة لكان الشيء حال عدمة موصوفاً بصفة وجوده وذلك محال (۱)
•
لا يقال : الجواب عن الإشكال الأول أن ذلك إنما يتوجه على من يقول الشيء حال وجوده وجوده ممكن الوجود أو حال عدمه ممكن العدم، أما من يقول حال وجوده يمكن أن يصير معدوماً في الزمان الثاني لا يلزمه هذا الإشكال .
وعن الثاني : أنه لا يلزم من صدق قولنا الماهية بشرط كونها موجودة غير قابلة للعدم صدق قولنا الماهية التي هي أحد أجزاء ذلك المجموع غير قابلة للعدم . و من الثالث : أن الإمكان وصف ثابت في الذمن لا تحقق له في الخارج، وعلى هذا التقدير لا يلزم ماذكرتم . لأنا نجيب عن الأول من وجهين : الأول أن القول بالإمكان الاستقبالى محال ، لأنا إذا حكمنا على الموجود في الحال بأنه يمكن أن يعدم فى الاستقبال فإما أن يقال إمكان المدم الاستقبالى حاصل في الحال ، أو يقال إمكان العدم الاستقبالى لا يحصل إلا في الاستقبال ، الأول محال ، لأن العدم فى الاستقبال من حيث إنه في الاستقبال موقوف على حصول الاستقبال ، وحصول الاستقبال محال في الحال فحصول العدم الاستقبالى من حيث إنه عدم استقبالى موقوف على حضور شرط محال والموقوف على المحال محالى ، فالعدم الاستقبالى ممتنع حضوره في الحال ، وإذا استحال حصول العدم الاستقبالى فى الحال لا يمكن حصوله إلا في الاستقبال كان إمكان حصوله حاصلا في الاستقبال لا في الحال .
•
·
فإن قلت: إنه وإن كان بهذا الشرط ممتنع الحصول في الحال لكنه غير ممتنع في الاستقبال ، ونحن إنما أثبتنا هذا الإمكان بالنسبة إلى الاستقبال قلت : الإمكان نسبة والنسبة لا توجد إلا بعد وجود المنتسبين . فالإمكان بالنسبة إلى الاستقبال لا يوجد إلا عند وجود الاستقبال فحصوله بالحال محال
•
معقولا منظوراً إليها لا آلة في النظر إلى غيرها وجدها عرضاً موجوداً فى محل هو عقله ممكن الوجود ، وهكذا الإمكان هو كآلة للعاقل بها يعرف حال الممكان فى أن وجوده كيف يعرض لماهيته ولا ينظر في كون الإمكان موجوداً أو غير موجود أو جوهراً أو عرضاً أو واجبا أو ممكنا ، ثم إن نظر في وجوده أو إمكانه أو وجوبه أو جوهريته أو عرضيته لم يكن بذلك الاعتبار إمكانا لشيء بل كان عرضاً فى محل هو العقل وممكنا في ذاته ووجوده غير ماهيته ، وإذا تقرر هذا فالامكان من حيث هو إمكان لا يوصف بكونه موجوداً أو غير موجود وممكنا أو غير ممكن وإذا وصف بثوء من ذلك لا يكون حينئذ إمكانا بل يكون له إمكان آخر فليحقق هذا حتى ينكشف حملة اعتراضات هذا الفاضل على الإمكان وعلى أمثاله وتزول الحيرة الذي عرضت له
. وتعرض لمن تقبع مقالته
(۱) قد مر أن الإمكان صفة للمتصور المسند إلى الوجود الخارجي والشيء حال عدمه يكون متصوراً
فيكون موصوفا بالإمكان
وأما الثانى : وهو أن يقال إمكان العدم الاستقبالى يحصل إلا عند حضور الاستقبال فهو محال أيضاً إذ كان ذلك حكما بالإمكان على الشيء بالنسبة إلى زمانه الحاضر ، لأن الاستقبال عند حضوره يصير حالا وحينئذ يعود أول الإشكال الثاني ، وإن سلمنا الإمكان الاستقبالى لكن الإشكال المذكور لا يندفع ، لأن قولنا إنه في الحال يمكن أن يصير معدوماً فى الاستقبال يقتضى إمكان صيرورة هريته محكوما عليها بالعدم ، ولو كانت هويته هين الوجود لمكان ذلك حكما باتصال الوجود بالعدم فيعود الإشكال المذكور (1)
وعن السؤال الثاني : أن شرط كون الشىء قابلا لشيء كون المقابل حالياً عما ينان المقبول ، فإذا كان وجود الماهية وعدمها ينافيان الإمكان، والماهية لا تخلو منهما فقد امتنع خلوها عما ينافي الإمكان فيمتنع اتصافها
بالإمكان (۲)
الثالث : أن حكم الذهن بالإمكان إما أن يكون مطابقا للمحكوم عليه أو لا يكون ، فإن لم يكن مطابقاً كان جهلا وكان حاصله أن الذهن حكم بالإمكان على ما ليس فى نفسه ممكنا ، وإن كان مطابقاً كان الشيء في نفسه متمكنا فيعود الإشكال المذكور فى أنه ثبوتى أو عدمى، ولأن إمكان الشيء وصف للشيء ، والذهني شيء آخر مغاير للشيء المحكوم عليه بالإمكان ، ووصف الشىء يستحيل قيامه بغير ذلك الشيء إلا أن يقال إن المراد من قولنا إمكان الشيء أمر حاصل فى الذهن ، أن العلم بالإمكان حاصل في الذهن وهذا حق ، لكنه لا يندفع السؤال ، لأن البحث واقع عن نفس الإمكان لا عن العلم بالإمكان (۳)
والجواب : أن كون الماهيات المتغيرة ممكنة لأمر ضروري ، والتشكيك فى الضروريات لا يستحق الجواب
هو الذى
(1) أقول : تصور الاستقبال في الحال معقول، والماهية لا من حيث هي موجودة أو غير موجودة مستندة إلى الوجود الخارجي في الاستقبال أو إلى عدمه ليست بمتعذرة التعقل ، والإمكان الاستثنائى يلحق ذلك المتصور عند ذلك الإسناد، والنظر فى أن إمكان العدم يحصل فى الحال أو في الاستقبال ليس نظراً في الإمكان من حيث كونه إمكاناً ، بل فيه أنه من حيث صوره في العقل وهو حاصل في وقت التعقل من صورة عقلية ومتعلق بالاستقبال من حيث هو إمكان ولا يلزم منه محال ، وأما أن الإمكان نسبة إضافية لا يتحقق إلا عند تحقق المنتسبين فقد ظهر أن منتسبه حاصل في التصور متعلق بالاستقبال . وأما قوله فى الوجه الثاني : لإمكان الامكان الاستقبالى، إن كان العدم الاستقبالى لا يحصل إلا عند حصول الاستقبال فباطل ، لأنه لا يتوقف على حصول الاستقبال بل يتوقف على تصور الاستقبال ، وما في كلامه معلوم الفساد بما مر .
(٢) أقول : الماهية لا تخلو من الوجود أو العدم فى الخارج، أما عند العقل فتخلو من اعتبارهما ، والإمكان صفة لها من حيث هي كذلك مسندة إلى الوجود أو إلى العدم. ( ۳ ) أقول : قد مر أن المطابقة أين تعتبر وأين لا تعتبر ، وتصور الإمكان ليس بحكم حتى يطابق فيه الوجود ، وإن اعتبر فيه المطابقة فيجب أن يكون مطابقة لما في العقل لأنه اعتبار عقلى كما مر ، والإمكان من حيث هو قائم بالذهن ليس بإمكان ، ومن حيث هو متعلق متصور لا بغير حصوله في الذهن ولا حصوله وهذا الخبط يعرض من عدم التمييز بين الاعتبارات العقلية والأمور الخارجية .
The second: that the originated thing before its existence is possible (mumkin) in itself. For if possibility (al-imkan) were an existent attribute, then the thing in the state of its non-existence would be described by an attribute of its existence, and that is impossible. 
•
Do not say: the answer to the first problem is that it is directed only against one who says that the thing in the state of its existence has its existence as possible existence or in the state of its non-existence as possible non-existence. As for one who says that in the state of existence it can become non-existent in the second time, this problem does not apply to him. 
And as for the second: that it does not follow from the truth of our statement 'the essence (al-mahiya) on condition of being existent is not receptive of non-existence' the truth of our statement 'the essence which is one of the parts of that composite is not receptive of non-existence.' 
And as for the third: that possibility (al-imkan) is an attribute subsisting in the mind (al-dhihn) with no realization in the external world. On this assumption, what you mentioned does not follow. 
We answer the first (objection) in two ways (wajhayn): The first: that the statement of future-directed possibility (al-imkan al-istiqbali) is impossible. For if we judge of the existent in the present that it can become non-existent in the future, then either it is said that the possibility of future non-existence is obtained in the present, or it is said that the possibility of future non-existence is only obtained in the future. The first is impossible because non-existence in the future, insofar as it is in the future, depends on the occurrence of the future. The occurrence of the future is impossible in the present. So the obtaining of future non-existence, insofar as it is future non-existence, depends on the presence of an impossible condition, and what depends on the impossible is impossible. Hence future non-existence is impossible to be present in the present. And if the obtaining of future non-existence is impossible in the present, and it cannot be obtained except in the future, then the possibility of its obtaining is obtained in the future, not in the present. 
•
·
If you say: It may be impossible to obtain in the present under this condition, but it is not impossible in the future, and we only affirmed this possibility with respect to the future. I say: Possibility is a relation (nisba), and a relation does not exist except after the existence of the two relata. So possibility with respect to the future does not exist except when the future exists, so its being in the present is impossible. 
•
Conceived as something considered, not as an instrument in reasoning about something else. You find it as an accident (arad) existing in a subject which is his intellect, and it is possible (mumkin) in existence. And thus possibility is like an instrument for the rational being by which he knows the state of the possible thing regarding how existence accrues to its essence. And he does not consider whether possibility is existent or non-existent, substance or accident, necessary or possible. Then if he considers its existence or its possibility or its necessity or its substantiality or its accidentalness, it is not in that respect a possibility for something, but rather it is an accident in a subject which is the mind (al-'aql), and it is possible in itself, its existence being other than its essence. And if this is established, then possibility insofar as it is possibility is not described as being existent or non-existent, possible or not possible. And if it is described with something from that, then it is not then possibility, but rather it has another possibility. Let this be verified, so that the burden of the objections of this [learned] man against possibility and its like may be revealed, and the confusion that has occurred to him may be removed. 
. And he is exposed to one whose discourse is base. 
(1) It has been mentioned that possibility is an attribute of the conceived thing (al-mutasawwar) that is attributed to external existence. And the thing in the state of its non-existence is conceived, so it is described with possibility. 
And as for the second: that it is said that the possibility of future non-existence is only obtained at the presence of the future. That is also impossible, since that would be a judgment of possibility upon a thing with respect to its present time. For the future when it becomes present becomes present, and then the first part of the second problem returns. And even if we admit future-directed possibility, the mentioned problem is not repelled, because our statement that in the present it can become non-existent in the future necessitates the possibility of its entity being judged by non-existence. And if its entity were firm in existence, that would be a judgment of connection of existence with non-existence, so the mentioned problem returns. (1) 
And as for the second question: that the condition of a thing being receptive of something is that the opposite be absent from that which receives. So if the existence and non-existence of the essence contradict possibility, and the essence is never free of them, then it is impossible for it to be free of what contradicts possibility, so it is impossible for it to be described with possibility. (2) 
The third: that the mind's judgment of possibility either corresponds to the object judged or does not. If it does not correspond, it is ignorance, and the result is that the mind judged possibility of what is not in itself possible. If it corresponds, then the thing is in itself possible, and the mentioned problem returns regarding whether it is positive (thubuti) or negative ('adami). And because the possibility of a thing is an attribute of the thing, and the mental thing is something else different from the thing judged with possibility. And it is impossible for an attribute of a thing to subsist in other than that thing, unless it is said that what is meant by our statement 'the possibility of a thing' is something obtained in the mind, and that the knowledge of possibility is obtained in the mind. This is true, but the question is not repelled, because the inquiry is about possibility itself, not about the knowledge of possibility. (3) 
And the answer: that the essences that change being possible is something necessary (dharuri). And raising doubts about necessary matters does not deserve an answer. 
It is he who... 
(1) I say: The conception of the future in the present is intelligible. And the essence, not insofar as it is existent or non-existent but attributed to external existence in the future or to its non-existence, is not impossible to conceive. And exceptional possibility (al-imkan al-istithnai) attaches to that conceived thing upon that attribution. And considering whether the possibility of non-existence obtains in the present or in the future is not a consideration of possibility insofar as it is possibility, but rather it is that insofar as you picture it in the intellect, it is obtained at the time of intellection as a mental picture and is related to the future insofar as it is possibility, and no impossibility follows from that. As for that possibility is a relational relation that is not realized except when the two relata are realized, it has become clear that its relatum is realized in conception and related to the future. And as for his statement in the second way: about the possibility of future-directed possibility—if future non-existence is only obtained when the future is obtained, that is false, because it does not depend on the obtaining of the future but rather on the conception of the future. And the corruption in his speech is known from what has passed. 
(2) I say: The essence is not free from existence or non-existence in the external world. As for in the mind, it is free from considering them. And possibility is an attribute of it insofar as it is thus, attributed to existence or to non-existence. 
(3) I say: It has passed that correspondence is sometimes considered and sometimes not. And the conception of possibility is not a judgment such that existence must correspond in it. And if correspondence is considered in it, then it must be correspondence with what is in the mind, because it is a mental consideration as has passed. And possibility insofar as it subsists in the mind is not possibility, and insofar as it is a related conceived thing, it is not without its being in the mind or its being. And this confusion arises from not distinguishing between mental considerations and external matters.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This is an extended argument defending the reality and nature of imkan (possibility) against a series of objections. The author begins by stating that the originated thing before its existence is possible in itself (mumkin li-dhatihi). He anticipates a critic's objection: if imkan were an existent attribute, then a thing in its non-existent state would have a positive attribute, which is absurd. The critic then lists three objections in the 'لا يقال' (do not say) block: 1) the first objection concerns whether imkan is regarding present or future states; 2) the second objection argues that if an essence on condition of existence is immutable, a part of that composite is not necessarily immutable; 3) the third objection claims imkan is merely a mental attribute with no external reality. 

The author then answers the first objection in two ways (وجهين). The first way argues that 'future-directed possibility' (الإمكان الاستقبالي) is impossible because the future non-existence does not exist in the present, so its possibility cannot be in the present. The critic then asks why not just affirm possibility with respect to the future. The author replies that imkan is a relation (نسبة) that only exists when both relata exist; hence future-directed possibility can only exist when the future exists. The author then elaborates that imkan is an instrument for the intellect, not an object of investigation about its own existence or nonexistence. It is an accident in the mind when considered, but the essence of imkan is not determined by external categories. The first footnote (1) reinforces that imkan attaches to mental conception attributed to external existence.

The second way answers that even if one accepts future-directed possibility, the problem returns because a present entity's future non-existence implies a connection between existence and non-existence in the same entity, which is contradictory. Then the author addresses the second and third objections. For the second, he argues that the condition for a thing to be receptive to something is that the opposite be absent; since existence and non-existence both contradict imkan, the essence cannot be free from them, so it cannot be described by imkan. For the third, he presents a dilemma: if the mind's judgment of imkan does not correspond, it is ignorance; if it corresponds, then the thing is in itself possible, raising again the problem of its status (positive or negative). The author then gives a definitive answer: that changing essences are possible is a necessary truth, and doubting necessary truths does not deserve a response. The final comments (أقول) provide further clarifications: the conception of the future is present in the mind; imkan relates to conceived attributes; the second way's argument is false because it depends on conception not actual future; the essence is free from existence/non-existence in the mind; and correspondence applies to mental considerations. The overall argument establishes imkan as a real, positive attribute of essences when considered in relation to existence or non-existence, not a mere mental fiction.

Key Terms
الإمكان
الممكن
الاستقبالي
النسبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that imkan is a property that can be predicated of a thing even when it doesn't exist, like a power or disposition.
Correction: Al-Razi shows that if imkan were a real attribute, it would require the thing to exist for the attribute to inhere. Since a non-existent thing cannot have attributes, imkan cannot be a real existent attribute. Instead, it is a relation or a mental consideration.

Checkpoint
Why does al-Razi argue that 'future-directed possibility' (الإمكان الاستقبالي) is impossible?
A) Because the future does not exist, so its possibility cannot be present.
B) Because possibility is a relation that requires both relata to exist, and the future does not exist now.
C) Because the mind cannot conceive of future non-existence.
D) Because the essence is immutable.

Key Takeaway
Future-directed possibility is impossible because possibility is a relation that requires the coexistence of its relata.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you often treat future possibilities as if they are already real in your mind, building hopes or fears on them? How does al-Razi's argument about the impossibility of future-directed possibility challenge you to reconsider the weight you give to what is not yet present? What would it mean for you to only rely on what actually exists now?
?
When you plan for the future, do you unconsciously assume that the possibility of success or failure is a real attribute of your current state? How does the idea that possibility is a relation requiring the existence of both relata force you to see your plans as grounded only in present realities? Will you still place your trust in future possibilities knowing they lack this relation?
?
Consider something you are hoping will happen next year. According to this lesson, that hope cannot be a real possibility now because the future does not exist. Does that unsettle you? How should your reliance on Allah's power and decree, rather than on abstract possibilities, change your approach to the future? What practical step can you take today to base your actions solely on what is present and certain?

Logic and Technical Terms

Further Defenses: Imkan as Instrument, Second Way, and the Ultimate Necessity
Al-Razi completes his defense of imkan with additional arguments and a final appeal to necessary truth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's additional arguments defending imkan, including the second way against the first objection, the answers to the second and third objections, and the final appeal to necessary truth.

Core Idea
Imkan is a necessary truth about essences that cannot be rationally doubted.

Having refuted the first objection in one way, al-Razi continues his defense. He describes imkan as an intellectual instrument, then provides a second way against the first objection. He then answers the second and third objections, and concludes by asserting that the possibility of changing essences is a necessary truth—any doubt about it is unworthy of response.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of imkan as an instrument
Read the paragraph starting with 'معقولا منظوراً إليها' to understand that imkan is not itself an object of investigation but a tool for reasoning.
Al-Razi emphasizes that imkan is an accident in the mind when considered, but its essence is not determined by external categories.
2
Follow the second way against the first objection
After the instrument paragraph, identify the second way (labeled 'وأما الثاني' in the translation). Al-Razi argues that even if future-directed possibility is admitted, the problem remains because it would connect existence and non-existence in the same entity.
This second way is a different angle: it shows that even if you accept the critic's notion, the original contradiction reappears.
3
Understand the answers to the second and third objections
Read the sections 'وعن السؤال الثاني' and 'الثالث'. For the second, al-Razi argues that since existence and non-existence both contradict imkan, the essence cannot be described by imkan. For the third, he presents a dilemma about correspondence and concludes that the conception of imkan is not a judgment.
These answers systematically dismantle the critic's remaining points.
4
Reflect on the final answer
Al-Razi concludes by stating that the possibility of changing essences is a necessary truth (ضروري) and that doubting necessary truths does not deserve an answer.
This is a strong epistemological claim: some truths are self-evident and require no proof.

الثالث : أن حكم الذهن بالإمكان إما أن يكون مطابقا للمحكوم عليه أو لا يكون ، فإن لم يكن مطابقاً كان جهلا وكان حاصله أن الذهن حكم بالإمكان على ما ليس فى نفسه ممكنا ، وإن كان مطابقاً كان الشيء في نفسه متمكنا فيعود الإشكال المذكور فى أنه ثبوتى أو عدمى، ولأن إمكان الشيء وصف للشيء ، والذهني شيء آخر مغاير للشيء المحكوم عليه بالإمكان ، ووصف الشىء يستحيل قيامه بغير ذلك الشيء إلا أن يقال إن المراد من قولنا إمكان الشيء أمر حاصل فى الذهن ، أن العلم بالإمكان حاصل في الذهن وهذا حق ، لكنه لا يندفع السؤال ، لأن البحث واقع عن نفس الإمكان لا عن العلم بالإمكان (۳)
والجواب : أن كون الماهيات المتغيرة ممكنة لأمر ضروري ، والتشكيك فى الضروريات لا يستحق الجواب

(1) أقول : تصور الاستقبال في الحال معقول، والماهية لا من حيث هي موجودة أو غير موجودة مستندة إلى الوجود الخارجي في الاستقبال أو إلى عدمه ليست بمتعذرة التعقل ، والإمكان الاستثنائى يلحق ذلك المتصور عند ذلك الإسناد، والنظر فى أن إمكان العدم يحصل فى الحال أو في الاستقبال ليس نظراً في الإمكان من حيث كونه إمكاناً ، بل فيه أنه من حيث صوره في العقل وهو حاصل في وقت التعقل من صورة عقلية ومتعلق بالاستقبال من حيث هو إمكان ولا يلزم منه محال ، وأما أن الإمكان نسبة إضافية لا يتحقق إلا عند تحقق المنتسبين فقد ظهر أن منتسبه حاصل في التصور متعلق بالاستقبال . وأما قوله فى الوجه الثاني : لإمكان الامكان الاستقبالى، إن كان العدم الاستقبالى لا يحصل إلا عند حصول الاستقبال فباطل ، لأنه لا يتوقف على حصول الاستقبال بل يتوقف على تصور الاستقبال ، وما في كلامه معلوم الفساد بما مر .
(٢) أقول : الماهية لا تخلو من الوجود أو العدم فى الخارج، أما عند العقل فتخلو من اعتبارهما ، والإمكان صفة لها من حيث هي كذلك مسندة إلى الوجود أو إلى العدم. ( ۳ ) أقول : قد مر أن المطابقة أين تعتبر وأين لا تعتبر ، وتصور الإمكان ليس بحكم حتى يطابق فيه الوجود ، وإن اعتبر فيه المطابقة فيجب أن يكون مطابقة لما في العقل لأنه اعتبار عقلى كما مر ، والإمكان من حيث هو قائم بالذهن ليس بإمكان ، ومن حيث هو متعلق متصور لا بغير حصوله في الذهن ولا حصوله وهذا الخبط يعرض من عدم التمييز بين الاعتبارات العقلية والأمور الخارجية .
The second: that the originated thing before its existence is possible (mumkin) in itself. For if possibility (al-imkan) were an existent attribute, then the thing in the state of its non-existence would be described by an attribute of its existence, and that is impossible. 
•
Do not say: the answer to the first problem is that it is directed only against one who says that the thing in the state of its existence has its existence as possible existence or in the state of its non-existence as possible non-existence. As for one who says that in the state of existence it can become non-existent in the second time, this problem does not apply to him. 
And as for the second: that it does not follow from the truth of our statement 'the essence (al-mahiya) on condition of being existent is not receptive of non-existence' the truth of our statement 'the essence which is one of the parts of that composite is not receptive of non-existence.' 
And as for the third: that possibility (al-imkan) is an attribute subsisting in the mind (al-dhihn) with no realization in the external world. On this assumption, what you mentioned does not follow. 
We answer the first (objection) in two ways (wajhayn): The first: that the statement of future-directed possibility (al-imkan al-istiqbali) is impossible. For if we judge of the existent in the present that it can become non-existent in the future, then either it is said that the possibility of future non-existence is obtained in the present, or it is said that the possibility of future non-existence is only obtained in the future. The first is impossible because non-existence in the future, insofar as it is in the future, depends on the occurrence of the future. The occurrence of the future is impossible in the present. So the obtaining of future non-existence, insofar as it is future non-existence, depends on the presence of an impossible condition, and what depends on the impossible is impossible. Hence future non-existence is impossible to be present in the present. And if the obtaining of future non-existence is impossible in the present, and it cannot be obtained except in the future, then the possibility of its obtaining is obtained in the future, not in the present. 
•
·
If you say: It may be impossible to obtain in the present under this condition, but it is not impossible in the future, and we only affirmed this possibility with respect to the future. I say: Possibility is a relation (nisba), and a relation does not exist except after the existence of the two relata. So possibility with respect to the future does not exist except when the future exists, so its being in the present is impossible. 
•
Conceived as something considered, not as an instrument in reasoning about something else. You find it as an accident (arad) existing in a subject which is his intellect, and it is possible (mumkin) in existence. And thus possibility is like an instrument for the rational being by which he knows the state of the possible thing regarding how existence accrues to its essence. And he does not consider whether possibility is existent or non-existent, substance or accident, necessary or possible. Then if he considers its existence or its possibility or its necessity or its substantiality or its accidentalness, it is not in that respect a possibility for something, but rather it is an accident in a subject which is the mind (al-'aql), and it is possible in itself, its existence being other than its essence. And if this is established, then possibility insofar as it is possibility is not described as being existent or non-existent, possible or not possible. And if it is described with something from that, then it is not then possibility, but rather it has another possibility. Let this be verified, so that the burden of the objections of this [learned] man against possibility and its like may be revealed, and the confusion that has occurred to him may be removed. 
. And he is exposed to one whose discourse is base. 
(1) It has been mentioned that possibility is an attribute of the conceived thing (al-mutasawwar) that is attributed to external existence. And the thing in the state of its non-existence is conceived, so it is described with possibility. 
And as for the second: that it is said that the possibility of future non-existence is only obtained at the presence of the future. That is also impossible, since that would be a judgment of possibility upon a thing with respect to its present time. For the future when it becomes present becomes present, and then the first part of the second problem returns. And even if we admit future-directed possibility, the mentioned problem is not repelled, because our statement that in the present it can become non-existent in the future necessitates the possibility of its entity being judged by non-existence. And if its entity were firm in existence, that would be a judgment of connection of existence with non-existence, so the mentioned problem returns. (1) 
And as for the second question: that the condition of a thing being receptive of something is that the opposite be absent from that which receives. So if the existence and non-existence of the essence contradict possibility, and the essence is never free of them, then it is impossible for it to be free of what contradicts possibility, so it is impossible for it to be described with possibility. (2) 
The third: that the mind's judgment of possibility either corresponds to the object judged or does not. If it does not correspond, it is ignorance, and the result is that the mind judged possibility of what is not in itself possible. If it corresponds, then the thing is in itself possible, and the mentioned problem returns regarding whether it is positive (thubuti) or negative ('adami). And because the possibility of a thing is an attribute of the thing, and the mental thing is something else different from the thing judged with possibility. And it is impossible for an attribute of a thing to subsist in other than that thing, unless it is said that what is meant by our statement 'the possibility of a thing' is something obtained in the mind, and that the knowledge of possibility is obtained in the mind. This is true, but the question is not repelled, because the inquiry is about possibility itself, not about the knowledge of possibility. (3) 
And the answer: that the essences that change being possible is something necessary (dharuri). And raising doubts about necessary matters does not deserve an answer. 
It is he who... 
(1) I say: The conception of the future in the present is intelligible. And the essence, not insofar as it is existent or non-existent but attributed to external existence in the future or to its non-existence, is not impossible to conceive. And exceptional possibility (al-imkan al-istithnai) attaches to that conceived thing upon that attribution. And considering whether the possibility of non-existence obtains in the present or in the future is not a consideration of possibility insofar as it is possibility, but rather it is that insofar as you picture it in the intellect, it is obtained at the time of intellection as a mental picture and is related to the future insofar as it is possibility, and no impossibility follows from that. As for that possibility is a relational relation that is not realized except when the two relata are realized, it has become clear that its relatum is realized in conception and related to the future. And as for his statement in the second way: about the possibility of future-directed possibility—if future non-existence is only obtained when the future is obtained, that is false, because it does not depend on the obtaining of the future but rather on the conception of the future. And the corruption in his speech is known from what has passed. 
(2) I say: The essence is not free from existence or non-existence in the external world. As for in the mind, it is free from considering them. And possibility is an attribute of it insofar as it is thus, attributed to existence or to non-existence. 
(3) I say: It has passed that correspondence is sometimes considered and sometimes not. And the conception of possibility is not a judgment such that existence must correspond in it. And if correspondence is considered in it, then it must be correspondence with what is in the mind, because it is a mental consideration as has passed. And possibility insofar as it subsists in the mind is not possibility, and insofar as it is a related conceived thing, it is not without its being in the mind or its being. And this confusion arises from not distinguishing between mental considerations and external matters.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This is an extended argument defending the reality and nature of imkan (possibility) against a series of objections. The author begins by stating that the originated thing before its existence is possible in itself (mumkin li-dhatihi). He anticipates a critic's objection: if imkan were an existent attribute, then a thing in its non-existent state would have a positive attribute, which is absurd. The critic then lists three objections in the 'لا يقال' (do not say) block: 1) the first objection concerns whether imkan is regarding present or future states; 2) the second objection argues that if an essence on condition of existence is immutable, a part of that composite is not necessarily immutable; 3) the third objection claims imkan is merely a mental attribute with no external reality. 

The author then answers the first objection in two ways (وجهين). The first way argues that 'future-directed possibility' (الإمكان الاستقبالي) is impossible because the future non-existence does not exist in the present, so its possibility cannot be in the present. The critic then asks why not just affirm possibility with respect to the future. The author replies that imkan is a relation (نسبة) that only exists when both relata exist; hence future-directed possibility can only exist when the future exists. The author then elaborates that imkan is an instrument for the intellect, not an object of investigation about its own existence or nonexistence. It is an accident in the mind when considered, but the essence of imkan is not determined by external categories. The first footnote (1) reinforces that imkan attaches to mental conception attributed to external existence.

The second way answers that even if one accepts future-directed possibility, the problem returns because a present entity's future non-existence implies a connection between existence and non-existence in the same entity, which is contradictory. Then the author addresses the second and third objections. For the second, he argues that the condition for a thing to be receptive to something is that the opposite be absent; since existence and non-existence both contradict imkan, the essence cannot be free from them, so it cannot be described by imkan. For the third, he presents a dilemma: if the mind's judgment of imkan does not correspond, it is ignorance; if it corresponds, then the thing is in itself possible, raising again the problem of its status (positive or negative). The author then gives a definitive answer: that changing essences are possible is a necessary truth, and doubting necessary truths does not deserve a response. The final comments (أقول) provide further clarifications: the conception of the future is present in the mind; imkan relates to conceived attributes; the second way's argument is false because it depends on conception not actual future; the essence is free from existence/non-existence in the mind; and correspondence applies to mental considerations. The overall argument establishes imkan as a real, positive attribute of essences when considered in relation to existence or non-existence, not a mere mental fiction.

Key Terms
الإمكان
الماهية
الذهن
الضروري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that imkan is a mental fiction without any basis in reality, or that it is a real property that can be independently investigated.
Correction: Al-Razi argues that imkan is a necessary attribute of essences when considered in relation to existence or non-existence. It is not a mental fiction; rather, it is a real relation that the intellect grasps. However, it is not an existent attribute in the way substances are.

Checkpoint
What is al-Razi's final answer to the objections?
A) He provides a logical proof that imkan is positive.
B) He states that the possibility of changing essences is a necessary truth and doubting it is not worthy of response.
C) He concedes that imkan is merely mental.
D) He appeals to revelation.

Key Takeaway
Imkan is a necessary truth about essences, and rational doubts against it are ultimately unanswerable because they question the self-evident.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider self-evident truths like the possibility of change in the world, do you ever find yourself doubting them? What does that doubt reveal about your reliance on reason versus revelation, and how can you strengthen your certainty in the foundational truths of your faith?
?
Al-Razi states that doubting necessary truths is not worthy of a response. Have you ever dismissed a core belief because it was challenged by a skeptic? Examine your own response: do you feel the need to defend at all costs, or do you humbly recognize some truths as foundational and beyond debate?
?
This lesson argues that imkan is a necessary truth about essences. Consider your own essence: do you truly believe that your existence is not necessary, that you are contingent? How does that realization shape your relationship with the Necessary Being (al-Wajib)?

Razi's Refutation of Causal Influence in Creatures
Razi argues that causal power cannot be a positive or negative attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's argument that causal influence (mu'aththiriyya) cannot be a positive or negative attribute and therefore cannot be ascribed to created beings.

Core Idea
Causal power in creatures is impossible – it is neither a positive attribute nor a negation without contradiction.

In this passage, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi presents a rigorous kalam argument against the notion that created beings possess genuine causal influence. He first shows that causal influence, being a relation, cannot be a substance; then he demonstrates that it cannot be a privative attribute either. The conclusion is that the very concept of creaturely causality is logically flawed.

Guided Path
1
Understand the first argument: causal influence is a relation, not a substance
Razi begins by asserting that causal influence is a relation between cause and effect. A relation cannot be a self-subsistent substance, so it cannot be an attribute of a substance. If it were additional to the essence, it would lead to infinite regress.
This argument targets the idea that causal power is a positive attribute inhering in the cause.
2
Examine the argument that causal influence cannot be a privative attribute
Razi argues that causal power is the opposite of non-causal power, which can be predicated of non-existence. The opposite of non-existence is existence, so causal power must be existent. Also, if a thing changes from non-influencer to influencer, the new attribute is positive.
This argument uses the logic of opposites and change to show causal power cannot be a negation.
3
Consider the analogy with knowledge
Razi uses the example of knowledge: if a being becomes knowledgeable, that knowledge is an existent attribute. Denying that would be absurd, so by analogy, causal influence must also be positive.
4
Synthesize the refutation
Since causal influence cannot be a positive attribute (due to the relation and regress arguments) and cannot be a privative attribute (due to opposite and change arguments), the notion of creaturely causal power is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
محال ، لأن مؤثرية الشيء في الأثر نسبة بين الأثر والمؤثر والنسبة بين الشيئين لا يعقل أن يكون جوهرا قائماً بالنفس . على تقدير التسليم فالمؤثر في وجود هذا الممكن هذا الجوهر أو ذاك أوهما ، وعلى التقديرات يكون مؤثرية ذات المؤثرة في وجود الممكن زائدة عليه ولزم التسلسل . وإنما قلنا : إنه لا يجوز أن يكون المؤثرية صفة عدمية لأنها نقيض الامؤثرية التي يصح حملها على العدم ، والمحمول على العدم عدم ونقيض العدم ثبوت ، فالمؤثرية أمر ثبوتى ، ولأن الشيء الذي لا يكون مؤثرا فصار مؤثراً فالمؤثرية حصلت بعد أن لم تكن فهى صفة وجودية، وإلا فليجوز فما إذا صارت الذات عالمة بعد أن لم تكن أن لا يكون العلم أمراً وجودياً وذلك نهاية الجبل له فظهر بما ذكرنا فسادكون المؤثرية صفة ثبوتية وكونها صفة عدمية، فإذا القول بالمؤثرية باطل .
Impossible, because the causal influence of a thing on the effect is a relation between the effect and the cause, and the relation between two things is not intelligible to be a self-subsistent substance. Granting that, then the influencer on the existence of this possible is either this substance or that, and in either case the causal power of the influencing essence in the existence of the possible would be additional to it, and an infinite regress would follow. And we said: It is not permissible for causal power to be a privative attribute, because it is the opposite of non-causal power, which can be predicated of non-existence; and what is predicated of non-existence is non-existence, and the opposite of non-existence is existence. So causal power is an affirmative thing. And because a thing that was not an influencer and then became an influencer — causal power occurred after it did not exist, so it is an existent attribute. Otherwise, it would follow that when a essence becomes knowing after not having been, that knowledge could be non-existent, and that is the utmost ignorance. So it is clear from what we have mentioned the corruption of causal power being an affirmative attribute or a privative attribute. Therefore, the statement of causal power is false.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a proof that causal influence (mu'aththiriyya) cannot be attributed to any creature. Razi begins by stating that causal influence is a relation between the cause and effect, and a relation cannot be a self-subsistent substance (jawhar qā'im bi-nafsih). Even if one grants that the cause is a substance, then its causal power would be additional to its essence, leading to infinite regress. Then he argues that causal power cannot be a privative attribute (ṣifa 'adamiyya), because it is the opposite of non-causal power, which is predicable of non-existence. The opposite of non-existence is existence, so causal power must be existent. Furthermore, if a thing changes from non-influencer to influencer, the causal power is a new attribute, hence positive. If one denies this, then by analogy, knowledge could be non-existent, which is absurd. Thus, causal power is neither purely affirmative nor privative in a way that avoids contradiction, so the entire notion of causal influence in creatures is refuted.

صفة عدمية
صفة وجودية
جوهر قائم بالنفس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think Razi denies all causality, including divine causality.
Correction: Razi specifically denies causal power to created beings, not to Allah; he is refuting the notion of independent creaturely causation.

Checkpoint

A) Because a privative attribute cannot be predicated of non-existence.
B) Because the opposite of non-causal power (non-existence) is existence, so causal power is positive.
C) Because privative attributes lead to infinite regress.
D) Because causal influence is a relation, not an attribute.

Key Takeaway
Razi demonstrates that the concept of creaturely causal influence is logically untenable because it fails both as a positive attribute (relation/regress) and as a privative attribute (opposite/change).

?
When you are stuck in a difficult situation, do you find yourself trusting more in a plan, a person, or a resource than in Allah? How does the logical impossibility of creaturely causal power expose that reliance as misplaced? What concrete step will you take this week to shift that trust?
?
If you truly believe that no created being has any causal influence, how does that change the way you view your own moral choices? Are you willing to accept that even your own will is not the ultimate cause of your actions? What does that mean for your accountability before God?
